management pattern based on the ConfigDef and ConfigKey classes for documenting and managing configuration parameters. This is not based on Java annotations as the task description suggests, but rather on a pattern of class-based configuration definitions.\\n\\n## Core Architecture\\n\\n**ConfigDef (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java)**: The primary class for specifying expected configurations. It contains a nested static class ConfigKey that represents individual configuration parameters. ConfigDef provides methods to define configurations with names, types, default values, documentation, validation logic, groups, ordering, and display information.\\n\\n**ConfigKey (nested in ConfigDef.java)**: A static inner class that encapsulates all metadata for a single configuration key, including: name, type (STRING, INT, LONG, DOUBLE, BOOLEAN, LIST, CLASS, PASSWORD), documentation, defaultValue, validator, importance (HIGH, MEDIUM, LOW), group, orderInGroup, width, displayName, dependents, recommender, internalConfig flag, and alternativeString.\\n\\n**AbstractConfig (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java)**: A base class that provides convenient methods for accessing configuration values. It holds a ConfigDef definition instance and provides methods like typeOf() and documentationOf() that retrieve metadata about configuration keys from the embedded ConfigDef.\\n\\n## Configuration Classes\\n\\nThe pattern is extensively used throughout Kafka across multiple modules:\\n\\n**Client Module**: AdminClientConfig, ConsumerConfig, ProducerConfig provide configuration for admin, consumer, and producer clients respectively.\\n\\n**Connect Module**: TaskConfig, WorkerConfig, ConnectorConfig, SourceConnectorConfig, SinkConnectorConfig, DistributedConfig, RestServerConfig, ConverterConfig define configurations for Kafka Connect components.\\n\\n**Mirror Module**: MirrorClientConfig, MirrorMakerConfig, MirrorConnectorConfig, MirrorCheckpointConfig, MirrorSourceConfig manage Mirror Maker configurations.\\n\\n**Streams Module**: StreamsConfig and AssignmentConfigs configure Kafka Streams applications.\\n\\n**Server Module**: ServerConfigs, AbstractKafkaConfig, ClientMetricsConfigs define broker-level configurations.\\n\\n**Other Modules**: GroupConfig manages consumer group configurations, LogConfig manages log-level configurations.\\n\\n## Utility and REST Support\\n\\nConfigUtils provides utility methods for working with ConfigDef instances. ConfigKeyInfo (in connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/) provides a REST-friendly representation of ConfigKey metadata. This is not based on Java annotations as the task description suggests, but rather on a pattern of class-based configuration definitions.\\n\\n## Core Architecture\\n\\n**ConfigDef (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java)**: The primary class for specifying expected configurations. It contains a nested static class ConfigKey that represents individual configuration parameters. ConfigDef provides methods to define configurations with names, types, default values, documentation, validation logic, groups, ordering, and display information.\\n\\n**ConfigKey (nested in ConfigDef.java)**: A static inner class that encapsulates all metadata for a single configuration key, including: name, type (STRING, INT, LONG, DOUBLE, BOOLEAN, LIST, CLASS, PASSWORD), documentation, defaultValue, validator, importance (HIGH, MEDIUM, LOW), group, orderInGroup, width, displayName, dependents, recommender, internalConfig flag, and alternativeString.\\n\\n**AbstractConfig (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java)**: A base class that provides convenient methods for accessing configuration values. It holds a ConfigDef definition instance and provides methods like typeOf() and documentationOf() that retrieve metadata about configuration keys from the embedded ConfigDef.\\n\\n## Configuration Classes\\n\\nThe pattern is extensively used throughout Kafka across multiple modules:\\n\\n**Client Module**: AdminClientConfig, ConsumerConfig, ProducerConfig provide configuration for admin, consumer, and producer clients respectively.\\n\\n**Connect Module**: TaskConfig, WorkerConfig, ConnectorConfig, SourceConnectorConfig, SinkConnectorConfig, DistributedConfig, RestServerConfig, ConverterConfig define configurations for Kafka Connect components.\\n\\n**Mirror Module**: MirrorClientConfig, MirrorMakerConfig, MirrorConnectorConfig, MirrorCheckpointConfig, MirrorSourceConfig manage Mirror Maker configurations.\\n\\n**Streams Module**: StreamsConfig and AssignmentConfigs configure Kafka Streams applications.\\n\\n**Server Module**: ServerConfigs, AbstractKafkaConfig, ClientMetricsConfigs define broker-level configurations.\\n\\n**Other Modules**: GroupConfig manages consumer group configurations, LogConfig manages log-level configurations.\\n\\n## Utility and REST Support\\n\\nConfigUtils provides utility methods for working with ConfigDef instances. ConfigKeyInfo (in connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/rest/entities/) provides a REST-friendly representation of ConfigKey metadata.
